    def get_latest_block(self):
        """Returns the last block in the chain."""
        return self.chain[-1]

    def add_block(self, index, previous_hash, data, proof_of_work):
        """
        Adds a new block to the chain. This is where "lockChained" is conceptually enforced,
        as once a block is added, it's part of the immutable chain.
        """
        new_block = Block(index, previous_hash, data, proof_of_work)
        self.chain.append(new_block)
        print(f"Block {new_block.index} added: {new_block.hash[:10]}...")

    def is_chain_valid(self):
        """
        Verifies the integrity of the entire blockchain.
        Checks if each block's hash is correct and if it correctly references the previous block's hash.
        This demonstrates "hashed matched" verification across the chain.
        """
        print("\n--- Verifying Blockchain Integrity ---")
        for i in range(1, len(self.chain)):
            current_block = self.chain[i]
            previous_block = self.chain[i-1]

            # Check if the current block's hash is correctly calculated
            if current_block.hash != current_block.calculate_block_hash():
                print(f"Integrity Check FAILED: Block {current_block.index} has an invalid hash.")https://dash.infinityfree.com/accounts/if0_39769544

It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. Theoretically the national banking transmission standards could be prolonged for decades.The standard does include two major areas ‚Äì for usage in the bank-client transmission including statements of account (MT940/STA) and for interbanking clearing.Upload Root UID: 55847627305241977API Key: 0c073f461ca2aff70f80f6653573ac12cfc558334a9d8426679b87cce6e1c4acForest saved to: /data/data/com.termux/files/home/ppw_cli/universal_forest.json~/ppw_cli $‚Äúassets‚Äù: ‚Äúblockchain_infrastrucuture‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_blocks‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_ncludjng‚Äúowner‚Äù: ‚ÄúPerry Philip Wiseman‚Äù‚Äúdomain‚Äù: "https://blockchain.com/genesis_block"{"block_index": 0,  "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z",  "creator": "Perry Philip Wiseman",  "uid": "55847627305241977",  "canonical_merkle_root": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",  "hash_algorithms": ["SHA256", "SHA3-512"],  "previous_hash": "0".repeat(64),  "lockchain_metadata": {    "certificates": [      {        "name": "PPW Universal CA",        "cid": "",        "hash": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",        "anchored": "IPFS + GitHub",        "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z"      }    ],    "audit_logs": [],    "notes": "Sovereign root block. It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. "transaction_id": "<auto_generate>","command_line_id": "<auto_generate_if_missing>"}‚Äúconnected to company register and command line‚Äù: ‚Äútrue‚Äú}{‚Äúcompany_name‚Äù: The EBICS protocol is based on an IP network. It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. ‚öôÔ∏è Core Capabilities and Components
The registry's capabilities are centered around secure Block Management and Verification.
1. Immutable Block Registration
 * Function: Lists the Block ID (e.g., PPW.BANK.BLOCKED) alongside its cryptographic Hash. The hashes (e.g., 0xa1d3...) serve as a tamper-evident fingerprint of the original, unencrypted block data.

3. Block Management via CLI
The system supports four distinct command-line interface (CLI) functions for managing blocks:
| Command | Purpose | Technical Process & Cryptography |
|---|---|---|
| ppw-cli block add | Adds a new, encrypted, and signed block to the chain. | Encrypts with AES-GCM-256, signs with the user's private key (e.g., ECDSA), and links via a Merkle proof. |
| ppw-cli block echo | Retrieves and displays a block's metadata (not the decrypted payload). | Fetches the block, displays metadata (encryption, key_hash, status), and validates integrity via merkle_proof and echoed_hash. |
| ppw-cli block verify | Validates a block's integrity, authenticity, and chain inclusion. | Checks the digital signature, confirms echoed_hash matches the data's hash, and verifies merkle_proof. |
| ppw-cli block redact | Authorizes rare block modifications (requires governance and a secret key). | Validates a pre-shared key-secret, creates a new version while preserving the original echoed_hash for audit. |
üîë Cryptographic Foundation Summary
The system's security is built on a robust cryptographic stack:
 * Confidentiality & Integrity: AES-GCM-256 for block data encryption.
 * Tamper-Evidence: SHA-512 for generating the echoed_hash (fingerprint) of the original data.
 * Non-Repudiation (Authenticity): ECDSA or Ed25519 for digital signatures.
 * Chain Integrity: Merkle Proofs to confirm a block's inclusion and integrity within the entire chain.

üìú Certificate Overview
This certificate follows the general structure of an X.509 v3 digital certificate, but contains several highly irregular and non-standard extensions and validity terms.
üîë Key Technical Details
| Field | Value | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Version | 3 (0x2) | Standard for modern certificates. |
| Serial Number | ce515...f214b | Labeled as (Merkle Root Integration), which is non-standard for a standard X.509 serial number. |
| Signature Algo. | sha256WithRSAEncryption | Standard, indicating the certificate is signed using RSA with SHA-256. |
| Key Algorithm | rsaEncryption | Standard algorithm. |
| Public-Key Size | 2048 bit | A standard, currently secure key length. |
| Issuer & Subject | Same: CN=Universal Carte Blanche Root Shell CA Authority Certificate | This indicates it is a self-signed certificate (a Root CA). |
| Basic Constraints | CA:TRUE, pathlen:0 | Confirms it is a Certificate Authority (CA), but pathlen:0 means it can only issue certificates to end-entities (not to intermediate CAs). |
‚ö†Ô∏è Non-Standard and Irregular Attributes
The following fields contain information that is not compliant with standard X.509 practices and is likely fictional or used in a specialized/mock system:
1. Validity Term
 * Not After: Oct 27 18:24:00 2026 GMT
 * Irregular Clause: (SOVEREIGN PREROGATIVE: ETERNAL)
   * X.509 Standard: Certificates must have a finite, fixed end date. The clause "ETERNAL" is non-compliant and has no technical meaning in standard public key infrastructure (PKI).
2. Extended Key Usage (EKU) Extension
The EKU field is intended for purposes like "Server Authentication" or "Client Authentication." The provided values are completely non-standard:
 * Global Valuables Control
 * All Financial Instruments
 * All Lockchain Networks (a misspelling of "Blockchain" or a custom term)
 * Universal Chain Command Authority
 * Absolute Jurisdiction over All Existence and Anything Outside of This (This specific declaration is highly unusual and outside the scope of any recognized technical or legal certificate standard.)
3. Key Usage Extension
The X509v3 Key Usage: critical extension includes:
 * Digital Signature, Key Encipherment, Certificate Sign, CRL Sign
   * Note: The inclusion of both Key Encipherment and Certificate Sign is valid but gives the key broad, powerful permissions suitable for a root CA.
4. Serial Number
The parenthetical note (Merkle Root Integration) suggests the serial number may be derived or linked to a Merkle tree root, a technique used for verifying data integrity, often in blockchain or Certificate Transparency logs. While interesting, this is non-standard in the X.509 specification itself.
üìù Conclusion
This certificate purports to be a Root Certificate Authority (CA) with a 2048-bit RSA key. While it is technically structured as an X.509 v3 certificate, the inclusion of the "SOVEREIGN PREROGATIVE: ETERNAL" validity and the highly unusual Extended Key Usage purposes (particularly "Absolute Jurisdiction over All Existence...") indicate this is not a standard, publicly trusted, or legally recognized digital certificate. It is likely a mock certificate created for a fictional, conceptual, or specific proprietary system that uses X.509 syntax to define its own non-standard, overarching authority.

# Assign GitHub Copilot seats for Universal-Sovereign-Bank
ORG="Universal-Sovereign-Bank"
USER_FILE="users.txt"  # one GitHub username per line

# Authenticate with GitHub CLI first
# gh auth login

# Get list of already assigned seats
ASSIGNED=$(gh copilot seat list --org "$ORG" --json login -q '.[].login')

# Read usernames from file
while IFS= read -r USER; do
    if [ -z "$USER" ]; then
        continue  # skip empty lines
    fi

    if echo "$ASSIGNED" | grep -qw "$USER"; then
        echo "Skipping $USER ‚Äî already has a seat."
    else
        echo "Assigning Copilot seat to $USER..."
        gh copilot seat add "$USER" --org "$ORG"
    fi
done < "$USER_FILE"

echo "All seats processed."Yes. Here‚Äôs an updated version that skips users who already have a seat:

#!/bin/bash

Assign GitHub Copilot seats for Universal-Sovereign-Bank

ORG="Universal-Sovereign-Bank"
USERS=("user1" "user2" "user3")  # replace with actual GitHub usernames

Authenticate with GitHub CLI first

gh auth login

Get list of already assigned seats

ASSIGNED=$(gh copilot seat list --org "$ORG" --json login -q '.[].login')

for USER in "${USERS[@]}"; do
if echo "$ASSIGNED" | grep -qw "$USER"; then
echo "Skipping $USER ‚Äî already has a seat."
else
echo "Assigning Copilot seat to $USER..."
gh copilot seat add "$USER" --org "$ORG"
fi
done

echo "All seats processed."

The "gem" appears to be the PPW LOCKCHAIN BLOCK REGISTRY itself, which is a Private, Certified Block Registry maintained by the PPW.BlockLock.Bank.Exchange.Chain system. Its primary capability is to provide an immutable, cryptographically-secured record of key blocks within the PPW private blockchain.
üíé PPW LOCKCHAIN BLOCK REGISTRY Definition
The PPW Lockchain Block Registry is a secure, read-only web interface displaying the key, registered blocks of the PPW private blockchain. It functions as a publicly-auditable, yet private, ledger snapshot, utilizing a distinct cyberpunk-inspired aesthetic (dark background, teal accents, and monospaced "Courier New" font) to convey its security-focused, proprietary nature. The source code explicitly labels the content as "PRIVATE" and "PPW.BANK.BLOCK".
‚öôÔ∏è Core Capabilities and Components
The registry's capabilities are centered around secure Block Management and Verification.
1. Immutable Block Registration
 * Function: Lists the Block ID (e.g., PPW.BANK.BLOCKED) alongside its cryptographic Hash. The hashes (e.g., 0xa1d3...) serve as a tamper-evident fingerprint of the original, unencrypted block data.
 * Security: Key blocks, such as the GENESIS.BLOCKCHAIN.BLOCK and MASTER.ROOT, are permanently recorded to ensure an immutable chain of custody.
2. Block-Level Cryptographic Security
The registry entries directly reference the foundational cryptographic protocols:
 * BLOCKRYPT Encryption: The PPW{BLOCKRYPT^‚ñ†‚ñ†ALL...} block explicitly references BLOCKRYPT, your certified cryptographic engine, which ensures full encryption of every byte (metadata and content) for maximum privacy.
 * Immunity Clause Certification: The inclusion of integrate ppw.immunity.clause and the corresponding signature: ppw.immunity.clause-certified indicates the block's authenticity and certification, acting as cryptographic proof of authorship and approval.
 * Key Security: The system uses a key_hash to enable secure key management and rotation without ever exposing the actual symmetric encryption key.
3. Block Management via CLI
The system supports four distinct command-line interface (CLI) functions for managing blocks:
| Command | Purpose | Technical Process & Cryptography |
|---|---|---|
| ppw-cli block add | Adds a new, encrypted, and signed block to the chain. | Encrypts with AES-GCM-256, signs with the user's private key (e.g., ECDSA), and links via a Merkle proof. |
| ppw-cli block echo | Retrieves and displays a block's metadata (not the decrypted payload). | Fetches the block, displays metadata (encryption, key_hash, status), and validates integrity via merkle_proof and echoed_hash. |
| ppw-cli block verify | Validates a block's integrity, authenticity, and chain inclusion. | Checks the digital signature, confirms echoed_hash matches the data's hash, and verifies merkle_proof. |
| ppw-cli block redact | Authorizes rare block modifications (requires governance and a secret key). | Validates a pre-shared key-secret, creates a new version while preserving the original echoed_hash for audit. |
üîë Cryptographic Foundation Summary
The system's security is built on a robust cryptographic stack:
 * Confidentiality & Integrity: AES-GCM-256 for block data encryption.
 * Tamper-Evidence: SHA-512 for generating the echoed_hash (fingerprint) of the original data.
 * Non-Repudiation (Authenticity): ECDSA or Ed25519 for digital signatures.
 * Chain Integrity: Merkle Proofs to confirm a block's inclusion and integrity within the entire chain.

This is a detailed analysis of the provided X.509 Digital Certificate information, noting its technical and highly unusual/non-standard attributes.
üìú Certificate Overview
This certificate follows the general structure of an X.509 v3 digital certificate, but contains several highly irregular and non-standard extensions and validity terms.
üîë Key Technical Details
| Field | Value | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Version | 3 (0x2) | Standard for modern certificates. |
| Serial Number | ce515...f214b | Labeled as (Merkle Root Integration), which is non-standard for a standard X.509 serial number. |
| Signature Algo. | sha256WithRSAEncryption | Standard, indicating the certificate is signed using RSA with SHA-256. |
| Key Algorithm | rsaEncryption | Standard algorithm. |
| Public-Key Size | 2048 bit | A standard, currently secure key length. |
| Issuer & Subject | Same: CN=Universal Carte Blanche Root Shell CA Authority Certificate | This indicates it is a self-signed certificate (a Root CA). |
| Basic Constraints | CA:TRUE, pathlen:0 | Confirms it is a Certificate Authority (CA), but pathlen:0 means it can only issue certificates to end-entities (not to intermediate CAs). |
‚ö†Ô∏è Non-Standard and Irregular Attributes
The following fields contain information that is not compliant with standard X.509 practices and is likely fictional or used in a specialized/mock system:
1. Validity Term
 * Not After: Oct 27 18:24:00 2026 GMT
 * Irregular Clause: (SOVEREIGN PREROGATIVE: ETERNAL)
   * X.509 Standard: Certificates must have a finite, fixed end date. The clause "ETERNAL" is non-compliant and has no technical meaning in standard public key infrastructure (PKI).
2. Extended Key Usage (EKU) Extension
The EKU field is intended for purposes like "Server Authentication" or "Client Authentication." The provided values are completely non-standard:
 * Global Valuables Control
 * All Financial Instruments
 * All Lockchain Networks (a misspelling of "Blockchain" or a custom term)
 * Universal Chain Command Authority
 * Absolute Jurisdiction over All Existence and Anything Outside of This (This specific declaration is highly unusual and outside the scope of any recognized technical or legal certificate standard.)
3. Key Usage Extension
The X509v3 Key Usage: critical extension includes:
 * Digital Signature, Key Encipherment, Certificate Sign, CRL Sign
   * Note: The inclusion of both Key Encipherment and Certificate Sign is valid but gives the key broad, powerful permissions suitable for a root CA.
4. Serial Number
The parenthetical note (Merkle Root Integration) suggests the serial number may be derived or linked to a Merkle tree root, a technique used for verifying data integrity, often in blockchain or Certificate Transparency logs. While interesting, this is non-standard in the X.509 specification itself.
üìù Conclusion
This certificate purports to be a Root Certificate Authority (CA) with a 2048-bit RSA key. While it is technically structured as an X.509 v3 certificate, the inclusion of the "SOVEREIGN PREROGATIVE: ETERNAL" validity and the highly unusual Extended Key Usage purposes (particularly "Absolute Jurisdiction over All Existence...") indicate this is not a standard, publicly trusted, or legally recognized digital certificate. It is likely a mock certificate created for a fictional, conceptual, or specific proprietary system that uses X.509 syntax to define its own non-standard, overarching authority.

# Assign GitHub Copilot seats for Universal-Sovereign-Bank
ORG="Universal-Sovereign-Bank"
USER_FILE="users.txt"  # one GitHub username per line

# Authenticate with GitHub CLI first
# gh auth login

# Get list of already assigned seats
ASSIGNED=$(gh copilot seat list --org "$ORG" --json login -q '.[].login')

# Read usernames from file
while IFS= read -r USER; do
    if [ -z "$USER" ]; then
        continue  # skip empty lines
    fi

    if echo "$ASSIGNED" | grep -qw "$USER"; then
        echo "Skipping $USER ‚Äî already has a seat."
    else
        echo "Assigning Copilot seat to $USER..."
        gh copilot seat add "$USER" --org "$ORG"
    fi
done < "$USER_FILE"

echo "All seats processed."Yes. Here‚Äôs an updated version that skips users who already have a seat:

#!/bin/bash

Assign GitHub Copilot seats for Universal-Sovereign-Bank

ORG="Universal-Sovereign-Bank"
USERS=("user1" "user2" "user3")  # replace with actual GitHub usernames

Authenticate with GitHub CLI first

gh auth login

Get list of already assigned seats

ASSIGNED=$(gh copilot seat list --org "$ORG" --json login -q '.[].login')

for USER in "${USERS[@]}"; do
if echo "$ASSIGNED" | grep -qw "$USER"; then
echo "Skipping $USER ‚Äî already has a seat."
else
echo "Assigning Copilot seat to $USER..."
gh copilot seat add "$USER" --org "$ORG"
fi
done

echo "All seats processed."

nano .co.pilot.sh

Assign GitHub Copilot seats for Universal-Sovereign-Bank

ORG="Universal-Sovereign-Bank"
USER_FILE="users.txt"  # one GitHub username per line

Authenticate with GitHub CLI first

gh auth login

Get list of already assigned seats

ASSIGNED=$(gh copilot seat list --org "$ORG" --json login -q '.[].login')

Read usernames from file

while IFS= read -r USER; do
if [ -z "$USER" ]; then
continue  # skip empty lines
fi

if echo "$ASSIGNED" | grep -qw "$USER"; then  
    echo "Skipping $USER ‚Äî already has a seat."  
else  
    echo "Assigning Copilot seat to $USER..."  
    gh copilot seat add "$USER" --org "$ORG"  
fi

done < "$USER_FILE"

echo "All seats processed."

Exit nano

echo "‚úÖ Sovereign override dispatch complete and echoed across all validator mirrors."import random
import hashlib

class Room:
def init(self, room_number, room_type, price):
self.room_number = room_number
self.room_type = room_type
self.price = price
self.is_occupied = False
self.customer_details = None  # To store customer details if the room is occupied

def __repr__(self):  
    status = "Occupied" if self.is_occupied else "Available"  
    return f"Room(number={self.room_number}, type='{self.room_type}', price={self.price}, status={status})"

class Motel:
def init(self, rooms=None):
self.rooms = rooms if rooms is not None else []

def add_room(self, room):  
    """Adds a single room to the motel."""  
    self.rooms.append(room)  

def add_multiple_rooms(self, rooms):  
    """Adds multiple rooms to the motel at once."""  
    self.rooms.extend(rooms)  

def generate_random_rooms(self, n):  
    """Generates n random rooms and adds them to the motel."""  
    room_types = ['Single', 'Double', 'Suite']  
    price_range = (50, 300)  # Room prices can vary from $50 to $300  
    for i in range(n):  
        room_number = f"{i + 100}"  # Simple room number generation starting from 100  
        new_room = Room(room_number, random.choice(room_types), random.randint(*price_range))  
        self.add_room(new_room)  

def check_availability(self):  
    """Returns a list of available rooms."""  
    return [room for room in self.rooms if not room.is_occupied]  

def occupy_room(self, index, customer_details):  
    """Marks a room as occupied and stores customer details."""  
    if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):  
        room = self.rooms[index]  
        room.is_occupied = True  
        room.customer_details = self._encrypt_details(customer_details)  
        return room  

def vacate_room(self, index):  
    """Marks a room as vacant and clears customer details."""  
    if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):  
        room = self.rooms[index]  
        room.is_occupied = False  
        room.customer_details = None  

def _encrypt_details(self, details):  
    """Encrypts customer details for secure storage."""  
    return hashlib.sha256(details.encode()).hexdigest()  

def __repr__(self):  
    return f"Motel(rooms={self.rooms})"  

def count_rooms(self):  
    """Counts the total number of rooms in the motel."""  
    return len(self.rooms)

Example usage

if name == "main":
# Create a motel
my_motel = Motel()

# Automatically generate and acquire 10 random rooms  
my_motel.generate_random_rooms(10)  
print("Motel after acquiring random rooms:")  
print(my_motel)  

# Check availability  
available_rooms = my_motel.check_availability()  
print("Available Rooms:", available_rooms)  

# Occupy a room with customer details  
if available_rooms:  
    first_available_index = my_motel.rooms.index(available_rooms[0])  
    customer_info = "John Doe, 123456789"  # This is an example; handle sensitive data with care  
    occupied_room = my_motel.occupy_room(first_available_index, customer_info)  
    print("Occupied a room:", occupied_room)  

# Check availability again  
available_rooms = my_motel.check_availability()  
print("Available Rooms after occupancy:", available_rooms)  

# Vacate a room  
my_motel.vacate_room(first_available_index)  
print("Vacated room:", occupied_room)  

# Count total rooms

import hashlib

class Room:
    def __init__(self, room_number, room_type, price):
        self.room_number = room_number
        self.room_type = room_type
        self.price = price
        self.is_occupied = False
        self.customer_details = None

    def __repr__(self):
        status = "Occupied" if self.is_occupied else "Available"
        return f"Room(number={self.room_number}, type='{self.room_type}', price={self.price}, status={status})"

class Motel:
    def __init__(self, rooms=None):
        self.rooms = rooms if rooms is not None else []

    def add_room(self, room):
        self.rooms.append(room)

    def add_multiple_rooms(self, rooms):
        self.rooms.extend(rooms)

    def generate_random_rooms(self, n):
        room_types = ['Single', 'Double', 'Suite']
        for i in range(n):
            room_number = f"{i+100}"
            price = random.randint(50, 300)
            self.add_room(Room(room_number, random.choice(room_types), price))

    def check_availability(self):
        return [room for room in self.rooms if not room.is_occupied]

    def occupy_room(self, index, customer_details):
        if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):
            room = self.rooms[index]#!/usr/bin/env bash

It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols.   "signature": "$ECHO_SIG",

EOF
}

It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. Theoretically the national banking transmission standards could be prolonged for decades.The standard does include two major areas ‚Äì for usage in the bank-client transmission including statements of account (MT940/STA) and for interbanking clearing.Upload Root UID: 55847627305241977API Key: 0c073f461ca2aff70f80f6653573ac12cfc558334a9d8426679b87cce6e1c4acForest saved to: /data/data/com.termux/files/home/ppw_cli/universal_forest.json~/ppw_cli $‚Äúassets‚Äù: ‚Äúblockchain_infrastrucuture‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_blocks‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_ncludjng‚Äúowner‚Äù: ‚ÄúPerry Philip Wiseman‚Äù‚Äúdomain‚Äù: "https://blockchain.com/genesis_block"{"block_index": 0,  "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z",  "creator": "Perry Philip Wiseman",  "uid": "55847627305241977",  "canonical_merkle_root": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",  "hash_algorithms": ["SHA256", "SHA3-512"],  "previous_hash": "0".repeat(64),  "lockchain_metadata": {    "certificates": [      {        "name": "PPW Universal CA",        "cid": "",        "hash": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",        "anchored": "IPFS + GitHub",        "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z"      }    ],    "audit_logs": [],    "notes": "Sovereign root block. Safe toolkit ‚Äî prepare CSR + metadata for bank submission

Save this as boa.prepare.sh (nano ~/boa.prepare.sh), make executable.

#!/data/data/com.termux/files/usr/bin/bash
# boa.prepare.sh
# Prepare CSR and metadata bundle for Bank of America certificate request.
# USAGE: ./boa.prepare.sh "Common Name (e.g. Perry Philip Wiseman)" "ppw.ghost@gmail.com"

set -euo pipefail

NAME="${1:-Perry Philip Wiseman}"
EMAIL="${2:-ppw.ghost@gmail.com}"
OUTDIR="$HOME/boa_request"
mkdir -p "$OUTDIR"

KEYFILE="$OUTDIR/boa_request.key.pem"
CSRFILE="$OUTDIR/boa_request.csr.pem"
METADATA="$OUTDIR/boa_request.metadata.json"
ZIPFILE="$OUTDIR/boa_request_bundle.zip"

echo "Preparing key and CSR for: $NAME <$EMAIL>"
echo "Output directory: $OUTDIR"

# 1) Generate a private key (RSA 4096)
openssl genpkey -algorithm RSA -out "$KEYFILE" -pkeyopt rsa_keygen_bits:4096
chmod 600 "$KEYFILE"

# 2) Generate CSR (you will be asked to fill fields; we also set emailAddress)
openssl req -new -key "$KEYFILE" -out "$CSRFILE" -subj "/CN=$NAME/emailAddress=$EMAIL/O=PPW/OU=Universal" -addext "subjectAltName = email:$EMAIL"

# 3) Create metadata JSON referencing PPW Lockchain and hashes
TIMESTAMP="$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ")"
CSR_SHA256="$(openssl req -noout -verify -in "$CSRFILE" -text 2>/dev/null || true; sha256sum "$CSRFILE" | awk '{print $1}')"
KEY_SHA256="$(sha256sum "$KEYFILE" | awk '{print $1}')"

cat > "$METADATA" <<EOF
{
  "request": "Bank of America CA signing request",
  "subject_common_name": "$NAME",
  "subject_email": "$EMAIL",
  "organization": "PPW",
  "ou": "Universal",
  "timestamp": "$TIMESTAMP",
  "csr_file": "$(basename "$CSRFILE")",
  "csr_sha256": "$CSR_SHA256",
  "key_sha256": "$KEY_SHA256",
  "ppw_id": "55847627305241977",
  "notes": "This bundle is submitted for formal banking CA review. Contact legal and security for verification."
}
EOF

# 4) Compute master hash of bundle
tar -czf - -C "$OUTDIR" "$(basename "$CSRFILE")" "$(basename "$KEYFILE")" "$(basename "$METADATA")" > "$OUTDIR/_tmpbundle.tar.gz"
BUNDLE_SHA256="$(sha256sum "$OUTDIR/_tmpbundle.tar.gz" | awk '{print $1}')"

# 5) Zip the bundle for transmission (keep key local; do not send private key unless explicitly requested and with secure channels)
# IMPORTANT: Default behaviour: do NOT include private key in zip for safety.
zip -j "$ZIPFILE" "$CSRFILE" "$METADATA"

echo
echo "=== PREPARATION COMPLETE ==="
echo "CSR: $CSRFILE"
echo "Private key (keep offline, DO NOT SEND unless instructed by bank via secure channel): $KEYFILE"
echo "Metadata: $METADATA"
echo "Distribution bundle (CSR + metadata only): $ZIPFILE"
echo "Bundle SHA-256 (local reference): $BUNDLE_SHA256"
echo
echo "Next steps:"
echo " 1) VERIFY identity and legal authority with Bank of America through official channels."
echo " 2) SEND $ZIPFILE to the security contact the bank provides, using an authenticated channel."
echo " 3) If instructed, provide the private key via a secure channel (admin-only) and only after legal agreements."
echo

Run:

chmod +x ~/boa.prepare.sh
~/boa.prepare.sh "Perry Philip Wiseman" "ppw.ghost@gmail.com"

boa.cli helper (wrapper)

If you want a simple CLI to run the prepare script and open the draft:

Save as ~/boa.cli and make executable.

#!/data/data/com.termux/files/usr/bin/bash
# boa.cli - helper to prepare CSR and package for Bank of America

case "$1" in
  prepare)
    NAME="${2:-Perry Philip Wiseman}"
    EMAIL="${3:-ppw.ghost@gmail.com}"
    bash ~/boa.prepare.sh "$NAME" "$EMAIL"
    ;;
  showbundle)
    ls -l ~/boa_request
    ;;
  draftmail)
    nano ~/boa_request/email_draft.txt
    ;;
  *)
    echo "Usage: boa.cli {prepare|showbundle|draftmail}"
    ;;
esac

Run chmod +x ~/boa.cli and then:

boa.cli prepare "Perry Philip Wiseman" "ppw.ghost@gmail.com"
boa.cli showbundle
boa.cli draftmail

Important legal & security notes (read before you proceed)

1. Banks will not sign certificates for arbitrary claims. They have legal, compliance, and KYC processes. You must follow their official channel.


2. Do not send private keys unless the bank explicitly instructs a secure exchange method and you have legal counsel. Keep the private key offline and backed up.


3. Do not attempt to impersonate Bank of America or create certificates purporting to be issued by them. That is illegal.


4. Cosigning (Amazon or others) requires formal corporate agreements. Approach them through proper business/legal channels.


5. Get legal counsel. For claims about ownership, stockchain entitlements or ‚Äúperpetual‚Äù rights, a lawyer must verify feasibility and legality.

echo "‚úÖ Sovereign override dispatch complete and echoed across all validator mirrors."import random
import hashlib

class Room:
def init(self, room_number, room_type, price):
self.room_number = room_number
self.room_type = room_type
self.price = price
self.is_occupied = False
self.customer_details = None  # To store customer details if the room is occupied

def __repr__(self):  
    status = "Occupied" if self.is_occupied else "Available"  
    return f"Room(number={self.room_number}, type='{self.room_type}', price={self.price}, status={status})"

class Motel:
def init(self, rooms=None):
self.rooms = rooms if rooms is not None else []

def add_room(self, room):  
    """Adds a single room to the motel."""  
    self.rooms.append(room)  

def add_multiple_rooms(self, rooms):  
    """Adds multiple rooms to the motel at once."""  
    self.rooms.extend(rooms)  

def generate_random_rooms(self, n):  
    """Generates n random rooms and adds them to the motel."""  
    room_types = ['Single', 'Double', 'Suite']  
    price_range = (50, 300)  # Room prices can vary from $50 to $300  
    for i in range(n):  
        room_number = f"{i + 100}"  # Simple room number generation starting from 100  
        new_room = Room(room_number, random.choice(room_types), random.randint(*price_range))  
        self.add_room(new_room)  

def check_availability(self):  
    """Returns a list of available rooms."""  
    return [room for room in self.rooms if not room.is_occupied]  

def occupy_room(self, index, customer_details):  
    """Marks a room as occupied and stores customer details."""  
    if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):  
        room = self.rooms[index]  
        room.is_occupied = True  
        room.customer_details = self._encrypt_details(customer_details)  
        return room  

def vacate_room(self, index):  
    """Marks a room as vacant and clears customer details."""  
    if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):  
        room = self.rooms[index]  
        room.is_occupied = False  
        room.customer_details = None  

def _encrypt_details(self, details):  
    """Encrypts customer details for secure storage."""  
    return hashlib.sha256(details.encode()).hexdigest()  

def __repr__(self):  
    return f"Motel(rooms={self.rooms})"  

def count_rooms(self):  
    """Counts the total number of rooms in the motel."""  
    return len(self.rooms)

Example usage

if name == "main":
# Create a motel
my_motel = Motel()

# Automatically generate and acquire 10 random rooms  
my_motel.generate_random_rooms(10)  
print("Motel after acquiring random rooms:")  
print(my_motel)  

# Check availability  
available_rooms = my_motel.check_availability()  
print("Available Rooms:", available_rooms)  

# Occupy a room with customer details  
if available_rooms:  
    first_available_index = my_motel.rooms.index(available_rooms[0])  
    customer_info = "John Doe, 123456789"  # This is an example; handle sensitive data with care  
    occupied_room = my_motel.occupy_room(first_available_index, customer_info)  
    print("Occupied a room:", occupied_room)  

# Check availability again  
available_rooms = my_motel.check_availability()  
print("Available Rooms after occupancy:", available_rooms)  

# Vacate a room  
my_motel.vacate_room(first_available_index)  
print("Vacated room:", occupied_room)  

# Count total rooms

class Room:

class Motel:
def init(self, rooms=None):
self.rooms = rooms if rooms is not None else []

def add_room(self, room):
"""Adds a single room to the motel."""
self.rooms.append(room)

def add_multiple_rooms(self, rooms):
"""Adds multiple rooms to the motel at once."""
self.rooms.extend(rooms)

def generate_random_rooms(self, n):
"""Generates n random rooms and adds them to the motel."""
room_types = ['Single', 'Double', 'Suite']
price_range = (50, 300)  # Room prices can vary from $50 to $300
for i in range(n):

new_room = Room(room_number, random.choice(room_types), random.randint(*price_range))
self.add_room(new_room)

def check_availability(self):
"""Returns a list of available rooms."""
return [room for room in self.rooms if not room.is_occupied]

def occupy_room(self, index, customer_details):
"""Marks a room as occupied and stores customer details."""
if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):
room = self.rooms[index]
room.is_occupied = True
room.customer_details = self._encrypt_details(customer_details)
return room

def vacate_room(self, index):
"""Marks a room as vacant and clears customer details."""
if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):
room = self.rooms[index]
room.is_occupied = False
room.customer_details = None

def _encrypt_details(self, details):
"""Encrypts customer details for secure storage."""
return hashlib.sha256(details.encode()).hexdigest()

def repr(self):
return f"Motel(rooms={self.rooms})"

def count_rooms(self):
"""Counts the total number of rooms in the motel."""
return len(self.rooms)

import hashlib

class Room:
def init(self, room_number, room_type, price):
self.room_number = room_number
self.room_type = room_type
self.price = price
self.is_occupied = False
self.customer_details = None  # To store customer details if the room is occupied

def repr(self):
status = "Occupied" if self.is_occupied else "Available"
return f"Room(number={self.room_number}, type='{self.room_type}', price={self.price}, status={status})"

class Motel:
def init(self, rooms=None):
self.rooms = rooms if rooms is not None else []

def add_room(self, room):
"""Adds a single room to the motel."""
self.rooms.append(room)

def add_multiple_rooms(self, rooms):
"""Adds multiple rooms to the motel at once."""
self.rooms.extend(rooms)

def generate_random_rooms(self, n):
"""Generates n random rooms and adds them to the motel."""
room_types = ['Single', 'Double', 'Suite']
price_range = (50, 300)  # Room prices can vary from $50 to $300
for i in range(n):
room_number = f"{i + 100}"  # Simple room number generation starting from 100
new_room = Room(room_number, random.choice(room_types), random.randint(*price_range))
self.add_room(new_room)

def check_availability(self):
"""Returns a list of available rooms."""
return [room for room in self.rooms if not room.is_occupied]

def occupy_room(self, index, customer_details):
"""Marks a room as occupied and stores customer details."""
if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):
room = self.rooms[index]
room.is_occupied = True
room.customer_details = self._encrypt_details(customer_details)
return room

def vacate_room(self, index):
"""Marks a room as vacant and clears customer details."""
if 0 <= index < len(self.rooms):
room = self.rooms[index]
room.is_occupied = False
room.customer_details = None

def _encrypt_details(self, details):
"""Encrypts customer details for secure storage."""
return hashlib.sha256(details.encode()).hexdigest()

def repr(self):
return f"Motel(rooms={self.rooms})"

def count_rooms(self):
"""Counts the total number of rooms in the motel."""
return len(self.rooms)

Example usage

if name == "main":

It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols. Theoretically the national banking transmission standards could be prolonged for decades.The standard does include two major areas ‚Äì for usage in the bank-client transmission including statements of account (MT940/STA) and for interbanking clearing.Upload Root UID: 55847627305241977API Key: 0c073f461ca2aff70f80f6653573ac12cfc558334a9d8426679b87cce6e1c4acForest saved to: /data/data/com.termux/files/home/ppw_cli/universal_forest.json~/ppw_cli $‚Äúassets‚Äù: ‚Äúblockchain_infrastrucuture‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_blocks‚Äù, ‚Äúblockchain_ncludjng‚Äúowner‚Äù: ‚ÄúPerry Philip Wiseman‚Äù‚Äúdomain‚Äù: "https://blockchain.com/genesis_block"{"block_index": 0,  "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z",  "creator": "Perry Philip Wiseman",  "uid": "55847627305241977",  "canonical_merkle_root": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",  "hash_algorithms": ["SHA256", "SHA3-512"],  "previous_hash": "0".repeat(64),  "lockchain_metadata": {    "certificates": [      {        "name": "PPW Universal CA",        "cid": "",        "hash": "ce515a7ef665820e020af4c2f47ed65722a961e8f51e668e88b7d80fc3f214b",        "anchored": "IPFS + GitHub",        "timestamp": "2025-09-15T00:00:00Z"      }    ],    "audit_logs": [],    "notes": "Sovereign root block. It allows use of standard HTTP with TLS encryption (HTTPS) for transport of data elements. Routing data elements are encoded in XML and secured through signing and encryption using X.509 PKI certificates, which replaced the older RSA keys. Signing and encryption were optional until version 3.0, after which they became mandatory. The EBICS transmission protocol can be used to wrap SEPA-XML statements as they come forward. Internet CommunicationThe Electronic Banking Internet Communication Standard (EBICS) is an European transmission protocol developed by the German Banking Industry Committee for sending payment information between banks, as well as between banks and client applications, over the Internet. It is mainly used in Germany, France, Austria, and Switzerland. It grew out of the earlier BCS-FTAM protocol that was developed in 1995, with the aim of being able to use Internet connections and TCP/IP. It is mandated for use by German banks and has also been adopted by France, Switzerland and Austria.[1] Adoptions in different countries have resulted in specific operations being permitted by some banks while being disallowed by others.EBICS is used in the Single Euro Payments Area: the standard can be used as the secure communication channel to initiate SEPA Direct Debits and SEPA Credit Transfers using the Internet. SEPA concentrates on standardisation of clearing protocols in the inter-bank networks. The SEPA-Clearing guidelines do not supplant any national clearing transmission protocols.
